0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">j</span>\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">w</span>\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">Lateral</a>\n</th>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">l</span>\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">l\xca\xb2</span>\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-right-width: 0;">&#160;</td>\n<td style="border-left-width: 0;">&#160;\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The voiceless plosives are pronounced with <a href="/wiki/Aspiration_(phonetics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aspiration (phonetics)">aspiration</a>. The dental, postalveolar and palato-velar plosives <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/t\xcc\xaa d\xcc\xaa t\xca\xb2 d\xca\xb2 k\xca\xb2/</span> are <a href="/wiki/Affrication" class="mw-redirect" title="Affrication">affricated</a> to <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[t\xcc\xaa\xcd\xa1\xce\xb8 d\xcc\xaa\xcd\xa1\xc3\xb0 t\xcd\xa1\xca\x83 d\xcd\xa1\xca\x92 k\xcd\xa1x\xca\xb2]</span> in many contexts.\n</p><p>Manx has an optional process of <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">lenition</a> of plosives between vowels, whereby voiced plosives and voiceless fricatives become voiced fricatives and voiceless plosives become either voiced plosives or voiced fricatives. This process introduces the <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">allophones</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xce\xb2 \xc3\xb0 z \xca\x92]</span> to the series of voiced fricatives in Manx. The voiced fricative <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xca\x92]</span> may be further lenited to <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[j]</span>, and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xa3]</span> may disappear altogether. Examples include:<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Voiceless plosive to voiced plosive</dt></dl>\n<ul><li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/t\xcc\xaa/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[d\xcc\xaa]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">brattag</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88brad\xcc\xaaa\xc9\xa1]</span> "flag, rag"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/k/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xa1]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">peccah</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88p\xc9\x9b\xc9\xa1\xc9\x99]</span> "sin"</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Voiceless plosive to voiced fricative</dt></dl>\n<ul><li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/p/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[v]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">cappan</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88kavan]</span> "cup"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/t\xcc\xaa/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xb0]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">baatey</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88b\xc9\x9b\xcb\x90\xc3\xb0\xc9\x99]</span> "boat"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/k/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xa3]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">feeackle</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88fi\xcb\x90\xc9\xa3\xc9\x99l]</span> "tooth"</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Voiced plosive to voiced fricative</dt></dl>\n<ul><li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/b/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[v]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">cabbyl</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88ka\xcb\x90v\xc9\x99l]</span> "horse"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/d\xcc\xaa/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xb0]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">eddin</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88\xc9\x9b\xc3\xb0\xc9\x99n\xca\xb2]</span> "face"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/d\xca\xb2/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xca\x92]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">padjer</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88pa\xcb\x90\xca\x92\xc9\x99r]</span> "prayer"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/d\xca\xb2/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xca\x92]</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[j]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">maidjey</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88ma\xcb\x90\xca\x92\xc9\x99], [\xcb\x88ma\xcb\x90j\xc9\x99]</span> "stick"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc9\xa1/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xa3]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ruggit</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88ro\xc9\xa3\xc9\x99t]</span> "born"</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Voiceless fricative to voiced fricative</dt></dl>\n<ul><li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/s/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xb0]</span> or <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[z]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">poosit</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88pu\xcb\x90\xc3\xb0it\xca\xb2] or [\xcb\x88pu\xcb\x90zit\xca\xb2]</span> "married"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/s/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xb0]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">shassoo</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88\xca\x83a\xcb\x90\xc3\xb0u]</span> "stand"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xca\x83/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xca\x92]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aashagh</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88\xc9\x9b\xcb\x90\xca\x92ax]</span> "easy"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xca\x83/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xca\x92]</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[j]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">toshiaght</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88t\xcc\xaa\xc9\x94\xca\x92ax], [\xcb\x88t\xcc\xaa\xc9\x94jax]</span> "beginning"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/x/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xa3]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">beaghey</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88b\xc9\x9b\xcb\x90\xc9\xa3\xc9\x99]</span> "live"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/x/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xa3]</span> &gt; \xe2\x88\x85: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">shaghey</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xca\x83a\xcb\x90]</span> "past"</li></ul>\n<p>Another optional process of Manx phonology is <a href="/wiki/Pre-occlusion" class="mw-redirect" title="Pre-occlusion">pre-occlusion</a>, the insertion of a very short <a href="/wiki/Plosive_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Plosive consonant">plosive consonant</a> before a <a href="/wiki/Sonorant_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Sonorant consonant">sonorant consonant</a>. In Manx, this applies to stressed monosyllabic words (i.e. words one syllable long). The inserted consonant is homorganic with the following sonorant, which means it has the same <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">place of articulation</a>. Long vowels are often shortened before pre-occluded sounds. Examples include:<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/m/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xe1\xb5\x87m]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">trome</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/t\xcc\xaaro\xcb\x90m/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[t\xcc\xaaro\xe1\xb5\x87m]</span> "heavy"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/n/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xe1\xb5\x88n]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">kione</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/k\xca\xb2o\xcb\x90n/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[k\xca\xb2o\xe1\xb5\x88n]</span> "head"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/n\xca\xb2/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xe1\xb5\x88n\xca\xb2]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ein</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/e\xcb\x90n\xca\xb2/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[e\xcb\x90\xe1\xb5\x88n\xca\xb2], [e\xe1\xb5\x88n\xca\xb2]</span> "birds"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc5\x8b/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xe1\xb6\xa2\xc5\x8b]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">lhong</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/lo\xc5\x8b/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[lo\xe1\xb6\xa2\xc5\x8b]</span> "ship"</li>\n<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/l/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xe1\xb5\x88l]</span>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">shooyll</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xca\x83u\xcb\x90l/</span> &gt; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xca\x83u\xcb\x90\xe1\xb5\x88l]</span> "walking"</li></ul>\n<p>The trill <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/r/</span> is realised as a one- or two-contact flap <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xbe]</span> at the beginning of syllable, and as a stronger trill <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[r]</span> when preceded by another consonant in the same syllable. At the end of a syllable, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/r/</span> can be pronounced either as a strong trill <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[r]</span> or, more frequently, as a weak fricative <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xb9\xcc\x9d]</span>, which may vocalise to a nonsyllabic <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x99\xcc\xaf]</span> or disappear altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> This vocalisation may be due to the influence of <a href="/wiki/Manx_English" title="Manx English">Manx English</a>, which is itself a <a href="/wiki/Non-rhotic_accent" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-rhotic accent">non-rhotic accent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Examples of the pronunciation of <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/r/</span> include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ribbey</i> "snare" <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88\xc9\xbeib\xc9\x99]</span></li>\n<li><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">arran</i> "bread" <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xcb\x88a\xc9\xbean]</span></li>\n<li><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">mooar</i> "big" <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[mu\xcb\x90r], [mu\xcb\x90\xc9\xb9\xcc\x9d], [mu\xcb\x90\xc9\x99\xcc\xaf], [mu\xcb\x90]</span></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels_2">Vowels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manx_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Vowels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The vowel phonemes of Manx are as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">\n<caption>Manx vowel phonemes\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th rowspan="2">\n</th>\n<th colspan="3"><a href="/wiki/Vowel_length" title="Vowel length">Short</a>\n</th>\n<th colspan="3">Long\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">Front</a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Central_vowel" title="Central vowel">Central</a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Back_vowel" title="Back vowel">Back</a>\n</th>\n<th>Front\n</th>\n<th>Central\n</th>\n<th>Back\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Close_vowel" title="Close vowel">Close</a>\n</th>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">i</span>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">u</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">i\xcb\x90</span>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">u\xcb\x90</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Mid_vowel" title="Mid vowel">Mid</a>\n</th>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">e</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">\xc9\x99</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">o</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">e\xcb\x90</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">\xc3\xb8\xcb\x90</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">o\xcb\x90</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Open_vowel" title="Open vowel">Open</a>\n</th>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">\xc3\xa6</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">a</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">\xc9\x94</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">\xc3\xa6\xcb\x90</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">a\xcb\x90</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">\xc9\x94:</span>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The status of <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xa6]</span> and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xa6\xcb\x90]</span> as separate phonemes is debatable, but is suggested by the allophony of certain words such as <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ta</i> "is", <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">mraane</i> "women", and so on. An alternative analysis is that Manx has the following system, where the vowels <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/a/</span> and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/a\xcb\x90/</span> have allophones ranging from <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x9b]/[\xc9\x9b\xcb\x90]</span> through <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xa6]/[\xc3\xa6\xcb\x90]</span> to <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[a]/[a\xcb\x90]</span>. As with Irish and Scottish Gaelic, there is a large amount of vowel allophony, such as that of <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/a/, /a\xcb\x90/</span>. This depends mainly on the \'broad\' and \'slender\' status of the neighbouring consonants:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">\n<caption>Manx vowel phonemes and their allophonic variation\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Phoneme\n</th>\n<th>"Slender"\n</th>\n<th>"Broad"\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/i/, /i\xcb\x90/</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[i], [i\xcb\x90]</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xaa], [\xc9\xaa\xcb\x90]</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/e/, /e\xcb\x90/</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[e]/[e\xcb\x90]</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x9b]/[\xc9\x9b\xcb\x90]</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/a/, /a\xcb\x90/</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x9b~\xc3\xa6]/[\xc9\x9b\xcb\x90~\xc3\xa6\xcb\x90]</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[a]/[a\xcb\x90]/[\xc3\xb8\xcb\x90]</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc9\x99/</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xa8]</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x99]</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc9\x99i/</span> (Middle Gaelic)\n</td>\n<td><span class="IPA">/u/, /u\xcb\x90/</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[u], [u\xcb\x90]</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xb8~\xca\x8a], [u\xcb\x90]</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/u\xc9\x99/</span> (Middle Gaelic)\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[i\xcb\x90], [y\xcb\x90]</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\xaa\xcb\x90], [\xc9\xaf\xcb\x90], [u\xcb\x90]</span>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>When stressed, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc9\x99/</span> is realised as <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xb8]</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Manx has a relatively large number of <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthongs</a>, all of them <a href="/wiki/Height-harmonic" class="mw-redirect" title="Height-harmonic">falling</a>:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">\n<caption>Manx diphthongs\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th rowspan="2" colspan="2">\n</th>\n<th colspan="3">Second element\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/i/</span>\n</th>\n<th><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/u/</span>\n</th>\n<th><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc9\x99/</span>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th rowspan="3">First <br />element\n</th>\n<th>Close\n</th>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">ui</span>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">i\xc9\x99 \xe2\x80\xa2 u\xc9\x99</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Mid\n</th>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">ei \xe2\x80\xa2 \xc9\x99i \xe2\x80\xa2 oi</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">eu \xe2\x80\xa2 \xc9\x99u</span>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Open\n</th>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">ai</span>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">au</span>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stress">Stress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manx_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Stress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Stress generally falls on the first syllable of a word in Manx, but in many cases, stress is attracted to a long vowel in the second syllable.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Examples include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">buggane</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/b\xc9\x99\xcb\x88\xc9\xa3e\xcb\x90n/</span> "sprite"</li>\n<li><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">tarroogh</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/t\xcc\xaaa\xcb\x88ru\xcb\x90x/</span> "busy"</li>\n<li><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">reeoil</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ri\xcb\x90\xcb\x88o\xcb\x90l/</span> "royal"</li>\n<li><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">vondeish</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/von\xcb\x88d\xcc\xaae\xcb\x90\xca\x83/</span> "advantage"</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Morphology">Morphology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manx_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Morphology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_consonant_mutations">Initial consonant mutations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manx_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Initial consonant mutations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Like all modern Celtic languages, Manx shows <a href="/wiki/Consonant_mutation#Celtic_languages" title="Consonant mutation">initial consonant mutations</a>, which are processes by which the initial consonant of a word is altered according to its <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(linguistics)" title="Morphology (linguistics)">morphological</a> and/or <a href="/wiki/Syntax" title="Syntax">syntactic</a> environment.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Manx has two mutations: <b><a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">lenition</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Eclipsis" class="mw-redirect" title="Eclipsis">eclipsis</a></b>, found on nouns and verbs in a variety of environments; adjectives can undergo lenition but not eclipsis. In the late spoken language of the 20th century the system was breaking down, with speakers frequently failing to use mutation in environments where it was called for, and occasionally using it in environments where it was not called for.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Initial consonant mutation in (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xca\x82/</span>\n</td>\n<td>h</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/h/ , /x\xca\xb2/</span>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" align="center"><i>(no change)</i>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-unatt-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-unatt_62-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-unatt_62-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-unatt_62-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-unatt_62-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-unatt_62-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-unatt_62-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-unatt_62-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-unatt_62-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-unatt_62-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Not attested in the late spoken language (Broderick 1984\xe2\x80\x9386, 3:66)</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div>\n<p>In the corpus of the late spoken language, there is also one example of the elipisis (nasalisation) of <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc9\xa1/</span>: the sentence <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">Ta mee er <b>ng</b>eddyn yn eayn</i> ("I have found the lamb"), where <i>ng</i> is pronounced <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/n/</span>. However, probably this was a mis-transcription; the verbal noun in this case is not <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">geddyn</i> "get, fetch", but rather <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">feddyn</i> "find".<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nouns">Nouns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manx_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Nouns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Manx nouns fall into one of two <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">genders</a>, masculine or feminine. Nouns are inflected for <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">number</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Plural" title="Plural">plural</a> is formed in a variety of ways, most commonly by addition of the suffix <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">-yn</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x99n]</span>, but also by vowel change, changing <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">-agh</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ax]</span> to <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">-ee</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[i\xcb\x90]</span> or <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">-eeghyn</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[i\xcb\x90\xc9\x99n]</span> or by adding other endings. There is usually no inflection for <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_case" title="Grammatical case">case</a>, except in a minority of nouns that have a distinct genitive singular form, which is formed in various ways. (Most common is the addition of the suffix <i>-ey</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x99]</span> to feminine nouns.) Historical genitive singulars are often encountered in <a href="/wiki/Compound_(linguistics)" title="Compound (linguistics)">compounds</a> even when they are no longer <a href="/wiki/Productivity_(linguistics)" title="Productivity (linguistics)">productive</a> forms; for example <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">thie-ollee</i> "cowhouse" uses the old genitive of <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ollagh</i> "cattle".<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> There are also traces of a dative singular in set phrases such as <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ry-chosh</i> "on foot", contrasting with nominative <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">cass</i> and genitive <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">coshey</i> (cf. <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">cullee choshey</i> "footwear", <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">bluckan coshey</i> "football, soccer, rugby").<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjectives">Adjectives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manx_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Adjectives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Certain adjectives have plural as well as singular forms (through the addition <i>-ey</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x99]</span>), although the use of the singular adjective with a plural noun is usual. Most adjectives end in <i>-agh</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ax]</span> and form their <a href="/wiki/Comparative" title="Comparative">comparative</a>/<a href="/wiki/Superlative" class="mw-redirect" title="Superlative">superlative</a> form by replacing this with <i>-ee</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[i\xcb\x90]</span>, e.g. <i>at\xc3\xa7himagh</i> "terrible" becomes <i>at\xc3\xa7himee</i>, giving <i>ny s\'at\xc3\xa7himee</i> "more terrible" and <i>s\'at\xc3\xa7himee</i> "most terrible". As in Irish and Scottish Gaelic, the comparative-superlative is commonly marked by the copula verb <i>s</i> (<i>is</i>) in the present, and <i>by</i> in the past; the superlative is often shown by the word "nys" /nis/, from Middle Irish <i>n\xc3\xad as</i> "thing that is" (cf. Irish <i>n\xc3\xados</i>, past <i>n\xc3\xad ba</i>). <sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> A number of adjectives form their comparative/superlative irregularly:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Irregular comparative/superlative forms of Manx adjectives\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Positive\n</th>\n<th>English\n</th>\n<th>Comparative/Superlative\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aalin</i>\n</td>\n<td>beautiful\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aaley</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aashag</i>\n</td>\n<td>easy\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">assey</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aeg</i>\n</td>\n<td>young\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aa</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ard</i>\n</td>\n<td>high\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language long\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">odjey</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">garroo</i>\n</td>\n<td>rough\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx text">gilley</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">giare</i>\n</td>\n<td>short\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">girrey</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">lajer</i>\n</td>\n<td>strong\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">troshey</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language lang="gv" title="Manx language text">lea</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">liauyr</i>\n</td>\n<td>long, tall\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language evil\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">messey</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">reagh</i>\n</td>\n<td>merry, lively\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">reaie</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">roauyr</i>\n</td>\n<td>fat, broad\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language lang="gv" title="Manx language text">thanney</i>\n</td>\n<td>thin\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">theinney</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ymmodee</i>\n</td>\n<td>many\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">lee</i>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The comparative/superlative can also be formed using <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">smoo</i> "more" with the positive form e.g. <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">s\'thrimmey</i> = <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">smoo trome</i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pronouns">Pronouns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manx_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Pronouns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In common with Irish and Scottish Gaelic, in addition to its regular personal pronouns, Manx has also a series used for emphasis. Under certain phonological circumstances, these can be used as unemphatic pronouns, e.g. "you were not" is <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">cha row uss</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[xa \xcb\x88rau \xca\x8as]</span> as <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">cha row oo</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[xa \xcb\x88rau u(\xcb\x90)]</span> sounds too similar to <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">cha row</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[xa \xcb\x88rau]</span> "they/he/she was not".\n</p><p>Notice the only difference between the masculine and feminine third person singular possessive pronouns is the <a href="/wiki/Consonant_mutation" title="Consonant mutation">initial sound change</a>, namely lenition and h-prefixing,  they cause, e.g. <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">e glioonag</i> "her laptop", <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">e ghlioonag</i> "his laptop", <i>e ooh</i> "his egg", <i>e hooh</i> "her egg".\n</p><p>An alternative to using the possessive pronouns is to precede a noun with the definite article and follow it with the inflected form of <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ec</i> "at" to show the person, e.g. <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">yn thie aym</i> "my house" (literally "the house at me") instead of <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">my hie</i> "my house". This is especially useful in the plural, where all persons share one possessive pronoun, e.g. <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">yn thie oc</i> "their house", as opposed to <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">nyn dhie</i> "our/your/their house".\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption><b>Manx personal pronouns</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th text">mee</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">mish</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">my</i><sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[1]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2">Second singular\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ou</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">uss</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dty</i><sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[1]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th rowspan="2">Third text">e</i><sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[1]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>feminine\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ee</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ish</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">e</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2">First plural\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">shin</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">shinyn</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">nyn</i><sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[2]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2">Second plural\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">shiu</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language plural\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ad</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">adsyn</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">nyn</i><sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[2]</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>1.<b><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">^</a></b> Causes lenition.\n</p><p>2.<b><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">^</a></b> Causes eclipsis.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verbs">Verbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manx_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Verbs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Manx verbs generally form their <a href="/wiki/Finite_verb" title="Finite verb">finite</a> forms by means of <a href="/wiki/Periphrasis" title="Periphrasis">periphrasis</a>: inflected forms of the <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_verb" title="Auxiliary verb">auxiliary verbs</a> <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ve</i> "to be" or <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">jannoo</i> "to do" are combined with the <a href="/wiki/Verbal_noun" title="Verbal noun">verbal noun</a> of the main verb. Only the <a href="/wiki/Future_tense" title="Future tense">future</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conditional_tense" class="mw-redirect" title="Conditional tense">conditional</a>, <a href="/wiki/Preterite" title="Preterite">preterite</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Imperative_mood" title="Imperative mood">imperative</a> can be formed directly by inflecting the main verb, but even in these tenses, the periphrastic formation is more common in Late Spoken Manx.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Examples:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption><b>Manx finite verb forms</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Tense\n</th>\n<th>Periphrastic form<br />(literal translation)\n</th>\n<th>Inflected form\n</th>\n<th>Gloss\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Present\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ta mee tilgey</i><br />(I am throwing)\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td>I throw\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Imperfect\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">va mee tilgey</i><br />(I was throwing)\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td>I was throwing\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Perfect\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ta mee er jilgey</i><br />(I am after throwing)<sup id="cite_ref-er_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-er-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td>I have thrown\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Pluperfect\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">va mee er jilgey</i><br />(I was after throwing)<sup id="cite_ref-er_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-er-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td>I had thrown\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Preterite\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ren mee tilgey</i><br />(I did throwing)\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">hilg mee</i>\n</td>\n<td>I threw\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Future\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">neeym tilgey</i><br />(I will do throwing)\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">tilgym</i>\n</td>\n<td>I will throw\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Conditional\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">yinnin tilgey</i><br />(I would do throwing)\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">hilgin</i>\n</td>\n<td>I would throw\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Imperative\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">jean tilgey</i><br />(Do throwing!)\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">tilg</i>\n</td>\n<td>Throw!\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Past participle\n</th>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">tilgit</i>\n</td>\n<td>thrown\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The future and conditional tenses (and in some <a href="/wiki/Irregular_verb" class="mw-redirect" title="Irregular verb">irregular verbs</a>, the preterite) make a distinction between <a href="/wiki/Dependent_and_independent_verb_forms" title="Dependent and independent verb forms">"independent" and "dependent" forms</a>. Independent forms are used when the verb is not preceded by any particle; dependent forms are used when a particle (e.g. <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">cha</i> "not") does precede the verb. For example, "you will lose" is <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">caillee oo</i> with the independent form <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">caillee</i> ("will lose"), while "you will not lose" is <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">cha gaill oo</i> with the dependent form <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">caill</i> (which has undergone <a href="#Initial_consonant_mutations">eclipsis</a> to <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">gaill</i> after <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">cha</i>). Similarly "they went" is <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">hie ad</i> with the independent form <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">hie</i> ("went"), while "they did not go" is <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">cha jagh ad</i> with the dependent form <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">jagh</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> This contrast is inherited from Old Irish, which shows such pairs as <i lang="sga" title="Old Irish language text">beirid</i> ("(s)he carries") vs. <i lang="sga" title="Old Irish language text">n\xc3\xad beir</i> ("(s)he does not carry"), and is found in Scottish Gaelic as well, e.g. <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">gabhaidh</i> ("will take") vs. <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">cha ghabh</i> ("will not take"). In Modern Irish, the distinction is found only in irregular verbs (e.g. <i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">chonaic</i> ("saw") vs. <i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">n\xc3\xad fhaca</i> ("did not see").\n</p><p>The fully inflected forms of the regular verb <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">tilgey</i> "to throw" are as follows. In addition to the forms below, a past participle may be formed using <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">-it</i>: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">tilgit</i> "thrown".\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption><b>Inflection of a regular Manx verb</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Tense\n</th>\n<th>Independent\n</th>\n<th>Dependent\n</th>\n<th>Relative\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Preterite\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">hilg</i>\n</td>\n<td>(same as independent)\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Future\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">tilgym</i><sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[1]</a></sup>, <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">tilgmayd</i><sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[2]</a></sup>, <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">tilgee</i><sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[3]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dilgym<sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[1]</a></sup>, dilgmayd<sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[2]</a></sup>, dilgee<sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[3]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dilgin</i><sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[3]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Imperative\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">tilg</i>\n</td>\n<td>(same as independent)\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>1.<b><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">^</a></b> First person singular, making the use of a following subject pronoun redundant\n</p><p>2.<b><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">^</a></b> First person plural, making the use of a following subject pronoun redundant\n</p><p>3.<b><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">^</a></b> Used with all other persons, meaning an accompanying subject must be stated, e.g. <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">tilgee eh</i> "he will throw", <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">tilgee ad</i> "they will throw"\n</p><p>There are a few peculiarities when a verb begins with a vowel, i.e. the addition of <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">d\'</i> in the preterite and <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">n\'</i> in the future and conditional dependent. Below is the conjugation of <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aase</i> "to grow".\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption><b>Inflection of a regular Manx verb beginning with a vowel</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Tense\n</th>\n<th>Independent\n</th>\n<th>Dependent\n</th>\n<th>Relative\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Preterite\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">d\'aase</i><sup><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">[1]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>(same as independent)\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Future\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aasym, aasmayd, aasee</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">n\'aasym, n\'aasmayd, n\'aasee</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aasys</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Conditional\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aasin, aasagh</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">n\'aasin, n\'aasagh</i>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Imperative\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aase</i>\n</td>\n<td>(same as independent)\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>1.<b><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">^</a></b> <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">d\'</i>  may also be spelt <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">j</i> when pronounced <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/d\xca\xb2/</span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[d\xca\x92]</span> i.e. before a slender vowel, e.g. "ate" can be either <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">d\'ee</i> or <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">jee</i>.\n</p><p>These peculiarties extend to verbs begins with f, e.g. <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">faagail</i> "to leave".\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption><b>Inflection of a regular Manx verb beginning with f</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Tense\n</th>\n<th>Independent\n</th>\n<th>Dependent\n</th>\n<th>Relative\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Preterite\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language title="Manx language text">faagym, faagmayd, faagee</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">vaagym, vaagmayd, vaagee</i>,\n<p><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">n\'aagym, n\'aagmayd, n\'aagee</i>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aagys</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Conditional\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">aagin, aagagh</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">vaagin, vaagagh</i>, <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">n\'aagin, n\'aagagh</i>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Imperative\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">faag</i>\n</td>\n<td>(same as independent)\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>1.<b><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">^</a></b> Again, <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">d\'</i>  may also be spelt <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">j</i> where appropriate.\n</p><p>A number of verbs are irregular in their inflection. \n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Inflected forms of lang="gv" title="Manx language text">nee\'m, neemayd, nee</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">jeanym, jeanmayd, jean</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">yinnin, yinnagh</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">jinnin, jinnagh</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">jean</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">jeant</i>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>1.<b><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">^</a></b> Future relative: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">clinnys</i>\n2.<b><a href="/wiki/Template:Ref_label" title="Template:Ref label">^</a></b> Future relative: <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">gowee</i>\n</p><p>The most common and most irregular verb in Manx is <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ve</i> "to be", often used as an auxiliary verb. In addition to the usual inflected tenses, <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ve</i> also has a present tense. The full conjugation of <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ve</i> "to be" is as follows.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Forms of verb <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ve</i> "to be"\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Form\n</th>\n<th>Independent\n</th>\n<th>Dependent\n</th>\n<th>Relative\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Present\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ta</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">vel, nel</i>\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Preterite\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">va</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">row</i>\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Future\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">bee\'m, beemayd, bee</i>\n</td>\n<td>(same as independent)\n</td>\n<td>vees\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Conditional\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">veign, veagh</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">beign, beagh</i>\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Imperative\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">bee</i>\n</td>\n<td>(same as independent)\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adverbs">Adverbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manx_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Adverbs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Manx adverbs can be formed from adjectives by means of the word <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dy</i>, e.g. <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">mie</i> "good", <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dy mie</i> "well";  <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">gennal</i> "cheerful", <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dy gennal</i> "cheerfully". This <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dy</i> is omitted when preceded by such words as <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ro</i> "too" and <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">feer</i> "very" or followed by <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dy liooar</i> "enough", e.g. <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">feer vie</i> "very good, very well", <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">gennal dy liooar</i> "cheerful(ly) enough". The adverb for "home(wards)" is formed with <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dy</i> and the noun <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">balley</i> "place, town, homestead" to give <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dy valley</i>, whereas the noun <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">thie</i> "house, home" can be used unchanged to convey the same meaning.\n</p><p>The language has a number of adverbs corresponding to English "up" and "down", the meaning of which depend upon such things as motion or lack thereof and starting point in relation to the speaker.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Manx adverbs expressing "up" and "down"\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>\n</th>\n<th>above the speaker\n</th>\n<th>below the speaker\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Stationary\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">heose</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ho\xcb\x90s/</span>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">heese</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/hi\xcb\x90s/</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Movement towards the speaker from\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">neose</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/no\xcb\x90s/</span>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">neese</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ni\xcb\x90s/</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Movement away from the speaker to\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">seose</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/so\xcb\x90s/</span>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">sheese</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xca\x83i\xcb\x90s/</span>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Examples of practical usage are <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">Ta dooinney heese y traid</i> "There\'s a man down the street" and <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">Ta mee goll sheese y traid</i> "I\'m going down the street", <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">Jean drappal neese</i> "Climb up (towards me)" and <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">Jean drappal seose</i> "Climb up (away from me)".\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prepositions">Prepositions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manx_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Prepositions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Like the other <a href="/wiki/Insular_Celtic_languages" title="Insular Celtic languages">Insular Celtic languages</a>, Manx has so-called <a href="/wiki/Inflected_preposition" title="Inflected preposition">inflected prepositions</a>, contractions of a <a href="/wiki/Preposition" class="mw-redirect" title="Preposition">preposition</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Pronoun" title="Pronoun">pronominal</a> direct object, as the following common prepositions show. Note the sometimes identical form of the uninflected preposition and its third person singular masculine inflected form.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Conjugation of Manx prepositions using pronominal ending\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="2">Person\n</th>\n<th><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ass</i><br />"out of"\n</th>\n<th><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">royd</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">voyd</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th rowspan="2">Third singular\n</th>\n<th>Masculine\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">oc</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">orroo</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">foue</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">huc</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">jeu</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">lhieu</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">maroo</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">roo</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">roue, rhymboo</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">voue</i>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In addition to the above "simple" prepositions, Manx has a number of prepositional phrases based on a noun; being based on nouns, the possessive personal pronouns are used to refer to what would in English be pronominal prepositional objects. This also happens in English phrases such as "for my sake".\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Conjugation of Manx prepositional phrases using possessive pronouns\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="2">Person\n</th>\n<th><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">erskyn</i><br />"above" (&lt; Middle Irish <i>for os ciond</i> \'on/at over head\')\n</th>\n<th><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">mychione</i><br />"concerning" (&lt; Middle Irish <i>um chiond</i> \'about/around head\')\n</th>\n<th><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">son</i><br />"for the sake of" (&lt; Middle Irish <i>ar son</i> \'on/for sake\')\n</th>\n<th><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">lurg</i><br />"after" (&lt; Middle Irish <i>lorg</i> \'track, trail, trace\')\n</th>\n<th><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">noi</i><br />"against" (&lt; Middle Irish <i>in aghaidh</i> \'in face DAT\')\n</th>\n<th><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">trooid</i><br />"through" (&lt; a Northern Gaelic nominalisation of the Middle Irish 3rd person singular preposition *<i>tromhaid</i> \'through him/it\', originally found as the article form, cf. Irish <i>tr\xc3\xadd an</i> \'through the\')\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2">First singular\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">er-my-skyn</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">my-my-chione</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">er-my-hon</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">my lurg</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">m\'oi</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">my hrooid</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2">Second singular\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">er-dty-skyn</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">my-dty-chione</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">er-dty-hon</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dty lurg</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dt\'oi</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">dty hrooid</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th rowspan="2">Third singular\n</th>\n<th>Masculine\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">er-e-skyn</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">my-e-chione</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">er-e-hon</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">e lurg</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">n\'oi</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">e hrooid</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Feminine\n</th>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">er-e-skyn</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">my-e-kione</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">er-e-son</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">e lurg</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">er-nyn-skyn</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">my-nyn-gione</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">er-nyn-son</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">nyn lurg</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">nyn oi</i>\n</td>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">nyn drooid</i>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Alternative conjugation patterns are sometimes found with these more complex prepositions using inflected prepositions, e.g. <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">mychione aym</i> for <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">my-my-chione</i> "concerning me", <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">son ain</i> "for our sake" instead of <i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">er-nyn-son</i> "for our/your/their sake".\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Numbers">Numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span t\xca\xb2i\xc9\x99k]</a></span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">feed</i>\n</td>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">fichead</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Help:IPA/Scottish Gaelic">[fi\xc3\xa7\xc9\x99t\xcc\xaa]</a></span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i lang="gv" title="Manx language
